We set the `release` parameter in javac and scalac\\n8: to `8` to ensure the generated binaries are compatible with Java 8 or higher (independently of the Java version\\n9: used for compilation). Java 8 support project-wide has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.0, Java 11 support for\\n10: the broker and tools has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.7 and removal of both is planned for Apache Kafka 4.0 (\\n11: see [KIP-750](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308223) and\\n12: [KIP-1013](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=284789510) for more details).\\n13: \\n14: Scala 2.12 and 2.13 are supported and 2.13 is used by default. Scala 2.12 support has been deprecated since\\n15: Apache Kafka 3.0 and will be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0 (see [KIP-751](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308218)\\n16: for more details). See below for how to use a specific Scala version or all of the supported Scala versions.\\n17: \\n18: ### Build a jar and run it ###\\n19:     ./gradlew jar\\n20: \\n21: Follow instructions in https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\\n22: \\n23: ### Build source jar ###\\n24:     ./gradlew srcJar\\n25: \\n26: ### Build aggregated javadoc ###\\n27:     ./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\\n28: \\n29: ### Build javadoc and scaladoc ###\\n30:     ./gradlew javadoc\\n31:     ./gradlew javadocJar # builds a javadoc jar for each module\\n32:     ./gradlew scaladoc\\n33:     ./gradlew scaladocJar # builds a scaladoc jar for each module\\n34:     ./gradlew docsJar # builds both (if applicable) javadoc and scaladoc jars for each module\\n35: \\n36: ### Run unit/integration tests ###\\n37:     ./gradlew test # runs both unit and integration tests\\n38:     ./gradlew unitTest\\n39:     ./gradlew integrationTest\\n40:     \\n41: ### Force re-running tests without code change ###\\n42:     ./gradlew test --rerun\\n43:     ./gradlew unitTest --rerun\\n44:     ./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\\n45: \\n46: ### Running a particular unit/integration test ###\\n47:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\\n48: \\n49: ### Repeatedly running a particular unit/integration test ###\\n50:     I=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \\\"Completed run: $I\\\"; sleep 1; done\\n51: \\n52: ### Running a particular test method within a unit/integration test ###\\n53:     ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\\n54:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\\n55: \\n56: ### Running a particular unit/integration test with log4j output ###\\n57: By default, there will be only small number of logs output while testing. You can adjust it by changing the `log4j.properties` file in the module's `src/test/resources` directory.\\n58: \\n59: For example, if you want to see more logs for clients project tests, you can modify [the line](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties#L21) in `clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties` \\n60: to `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO` and then run:\\n61:     \\n62:     ./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest   \\n63: \\n64: And you should see `INFO` level logs in the file under the `clients/build/test-results/test` directory.\\n65: \\n66: ### Specifying test retries ###\\n67: By default, each failed test is retried once up to a maximum of five retries per test run. Tests are retried at the end of the test task. Adjust these parameters in the following way:\\n68: \\n69:     ./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\\n70:     \\n71: See [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\\n72: \\n73: ### Generating test coverage reports ###\\n74: Generate coverage reports for the whole project:\\n75: \\n76:     ./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\\n77: \\n78: Generate coverage for a single module, i.e.: \\n79: \\n80:     ./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\\n81:     \\n82: ### Building a binary release gzipped tar ball ###\\n83:     ./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\\n84: \\n85: The release file can be found inside `./core/build/distributions/`.\\n86: \\n87: ### Building auto generated messages ###\\n88: Sometimes it is only necessary to rebuild the RPC auto-generated message data when switching between branches, as they could\\n89: fail due to code changes. You can just run:\\n90:  \\n91:     ./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\\n92: \\n93: ### Running a Kafka broker in KRaft mode\\n94: \\n95: Using compiled files:\\n96: \\n97:     KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID=\\\"$(./bin/kafka-storage.sh random-uuid)\\\"\\n98:     ./bin/kafka-storage.sh format -t $KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID -c config/kraft/server.properties\\n99:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/kraft/server.properties\\n100: \\n101: Using docker image:\\n102: \\n103:     docker run -p 9092:9092 apache/kafka:3.7.0\\n104: \\n105: ### Running a Kafka broker in ZooKeeper mode\\n106: \\n107: Using compiled files:\\n108: \\n109:     ./bin/zookeeper-server-start.sh config/zookeeper.properties\\n110:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/server.properties\\n111: \\n112: >Since ZooKeeper mode is already deprecated and planned to be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0, the docker image only supports running in KRaft mode\\n113: \\n114: ### Cleaning the build ###\\n115:     ./gradlew clean\\n116: \\n117: ### Running a task with one of the Scala versions available (2.12.x or 2.13.x) ###\\n118: *Note that if building the jars with a version other than 2.13.x, you need to set the `SCALA_VERSION` variable or change it in `bin/kafka-run-class.sh` to run the quick start.*\\n119: \\n120: You can pass either the major version (eg 2.12) or the full version (eg 2.12.7):\\n121: \\n122:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\\n123:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 test\\n124:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 releaseTarGz\\n125: \\n126: ### Running a task with all the scala versions enabled by default ###\\n127: \\n128: Invoke the `gradlewAll` script followed by the task(s):\\n129: \\n130:     ./gradlewAll test\\n131:     ./gradlewAll jar\\n132:     ./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\\n133: \\n134: ### Running a task for a specific project ###\\n135: This is for `core`, `examples` and `clients`\\n136: \\n137:     ./gradlew core:jar\\n138:     ./gradlew core:test\\n139: \\n140: Streams has multiple sub-projects, but you can run all the tests:\\n141: \\n142:     ./gradlew :streams:testAll\\n143: \\n144: ### Listing all gradle tasks ###\\n145:     ./gradlew tasks\\n146: \\n147: ### Building IDE project ####\\n148: *Note that this is not strictly necessary (IntelliJ IDEA has good built-in support for Gradle projects, for example).*\\n149: \\n150:     ./gradlew eclipse\\n151:     ./gradlew idea\\n152: \\n153: The `eclipse` task has been configured to use `${project_dir}/build_eclipse` as Eclipse's build directory. Eclipse's default\\n154: build directory (`${project_dir}/bin`) clashes with Kafka's scripts directory and we don't use Gradle's build directory\\n155: to avoid known issues with this repository ###\\n206: The recommended command to build for both Scala 2.12 and 2.13 is:\\n207: \\n208:     ./gradlewAll publishToMavenLocal\\n209: \\n210: For backwards compatibility, the following testJar\\n222: \\n223: ### Running code quality checks ###\\n224: There are two code quality analysis tools that we regularly run, spotbugs and checkstyle.\\n225: \\n226: #### Checkstyle ####\\n227: Checkstyle enforces a consistent coding style in Kafka.\\n228: You can run checkstyle using:\\n229: \\n230:     ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\\n231: \\n232: The checkstyle warnings will be found in `reports/checkstyle/reports/main.html` and `reports/checkstyle/reports/test.html` files in the\\n233: subproject build directories. They are also printed to the console. The build will fail if Checkstyle fails.\\n234: \\n235: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessCheck` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\\n236: \\n237: #### Spotless ####\\n238: The import order is a part of static check. please call `spotlessApply` (require JDK 11+) to optimize the imports of Java codes before filing pull request.\\n239: \\n240:     ./gradlew spotlessApply\\n241: \\n242: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessApply` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\\n243: \\n244: #### Spotbugs ####\\n245: Spotbugs uses static analysis to look for bugs in the code.\\n246: You can run spotbugs using:\\n247: \\n248:     ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\\n249: \\n250: The spotbugs warnings will be found in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `reports/spotbugs/test.html` files in the subproject build\\n251: directories.  Use -PxmlSpotBugsReport=true to generate an XML report instead of an HTML one.\\n252: \\n253: ### JMH microbenchmarks ###\\n254: We use [JMH](https://openjdk.java.net/projects/code-tools/jmh/) to write microbenchmarks that produce reliable results in the JVM.\\n255:     \\n256: See [jmh-benchmarks/README.md](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/jmh-benchmarks/README.md) for details on how to run the microbenchmarks.\\n257: \\n258: ### Dependency Analysis ###\\n259: \\n260: The gradle [dependency debugging documentation](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/viewing_debugging_dependencies.html) mentions using the `dependencies` or `dependencyInsight` tasks to debug dependencies for the root project or individual subprojects.\\n261: \\n262: Alternatively, use the `allDeps` or `allDepInsight` tasks for recursively iterating through all subprojects:\\n263: \\n264:     ./gradlew allDeps\\n265: \\n266:     ./gradlew allDepInsight --configuration runtimeClasspath --dependency com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind\\n267: \\n268: These take the same arguments as the builtin variants.\\n269: \\n270: ### Determining if any dependencies could be updated ###\\n271:     ./gradlew dependencyUpdates\\n272: \\n273: ### Common build options ###\\n274: \\n275: The following options should be set with a `-P` switch, for example `./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=1 test`.\\n276: \\n277: * `commitId`: sets the build commit ID as .git/HEAD might not be correct if there are local commits added for build purposes.\\n278: * `mavenUrl`: sets the URL of the maven deployment repository (`file://path/to/repo` can be used to point to a local repository).\\n279: * `maxParallelForks`: maximum number of test processes to start in parallel. Defaults to the number of processors available to the JVM.\\n280: * `maxScalacThreads`: maximum number of worker threads for the scalac backend. Defaults to the lowest of `8` and the number of processors\\n281: available to the JVM. The value must be between 1 and 16 (inclusive). \\n282: * `ignoreFailures`: ignore test failures from junit\\n283: * `showStandardStreams`: shows standard out and standard error of the test JVM(s) on the console.\\n284: * `skipSigning`: skips signing of artifacts.\\n285: * `testLoggingEvents`: unit test events to be logged, separated by comma. For example `./gradlew -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed test`.\\n286: * `xmlSpotBugsReport`: enable XML reports for spotBugs. This also disables HTML reports as only one can be enabled at a time.\\n287: * `maxTestRetries`: maximum number of retries for a failing test case.\\n288: * `maxTestRetryFailures`: maximum number of test failures before retrying is disabled for subsequent tests.\\n289: * `enableTestCoverage`: enables test coverage plugins and tasks, including bytecode enhancement of classes required to track said\\n290: coverage. Note that this introduces some overhead when running tests and hence why it's disabled by default (the overhead\\n291: varies, but 15-20% is a reasonable estimate).\\n292: * `keepAliveMode`: configures the keep alive mode for the Gradle compilation daemon - reuse improves start-up time. The values should \\n293: be one of `daemon` or `session` (the default is `daemon`). `daemon` keeps the daemon alive until it's explicitly stopped while\\n294: `session` keeps it alive until the end of the build session. This currently only affects the Scala compiler, see\\n295: https://github.com/gradle/gradle/pull/21034 for a PR that attempts to do the same for the Java compiler.\\n296: * `scalaOptimizerMode`: configures the optimizing behavior of the scala compiler, the value should be one of `none`, `method`, `inline-kafka` or\\n297: `inline-scala` (the default is `inline-kafka`). `none` is the scala compiler default, which only eliminates unreachable code. `method` also\\n298: includes method-local optimizations. `inline-kafka` adds inlining of methods within the kafka packages. Finally, `inline-scala` also\\n299: includes inlining of methods within the scala library (which avoids lambda allocations for methods like `Option.exists`). `inline-scala` is\\n300: only safe if the Scala library version is the same at compile time and runtime. Since we cannot guarantee this for all cases (for example, users\\n301: may depend on the kafka jar for integration tests where they may include a scala library with a different version), we don't enable it by\\n302: default. See https://www.lightbend.com/blog/scala-inliner-optimizer for more details.\\n303: \\n304: ### Running system tests ###\\n305: \\n306: See [tests/README.md](tests/README.md).\\n307: \\n308: ### Running in Vagrant ###\\n309: \\n310: See [vagrant/README.md](vagrant/README.md).\\n311: \\n312: ### Contribution ###\\n313: \\n314: Apache Kafka is interested in building the community; we would welcome any thoughts or [patches](https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA). We set the `release` parameter in javac and scalac\\n8: to `8` to ensure the generated binaries are compatible with Java 8 or higher (independently of the Java version\\n9: used for compilation). Java 8 support project-wide has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.0, Java 11 support for\\n10: the broker and tools has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.7 and removal of both is planned for Apache Kafka 4.0 (\\n11: see [KIP-750](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308223) and\\n12: [KIP-1013](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=284789510) for more details).\\n13: \\n14: Scala 2.12 and 2.13 are supported and 2.13 is used by default. Scala 2.12 support has been deprecated since\\n15: Apache Kafka 3.0 and will be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0 (see [KIP-751](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308218)\\n16: for more details). See below for how to use a specific Scala version or all of the supported Scala versions.\\n17: \\n18: ### Build a jar and run it ###\\n19:     ./gradlew jar\\n20: \\n21: Follow instructions in https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\\n22: \\n23: ### Build source jar ###\\n24:     ./gradlew srcJar\\n25: \\n26: ### Build aggregated javadoc ###\\n27:     ./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\\n28: \\n29: ### Build javadoc and scaladoc ###\\n30:     ./gradlew javadoc\\n31:     ./gradlew javadocJar # builds a javadoc jar for each module\\n32:     ./gradlew scaladoc\\n33:     ./gradlew scaladocJar # builds a scaladoc jar for each module\\n34:     ./gradlew docsJar # builds both (if applicable) javadoc and scaladoc jars for each module\\n35: \\n36: ### Run unit/integration tests ###\\n37:     ./gradlew test # runs both unit and integration tests\\n38:     ./gradlew unitTest\\n39:     ./gradlew integrationTest\\n40:     \\n41: ### Force re-running tests without code change ###\\n42:     ./gradlew test --rerun\\n43:     ./gradlew unitTest --rerun\\n44:     ./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\\n45: \\n46: ### Running a particular unit/integration test ###\\n47:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\\n48: \\n49: ### Repeatedly running a particular unit/integration test ###\\n50:     I=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \\\"Completed run: $I\\\"; sleep 1; done\\n51: \\n52: ### Running a particular test method within a unit/integration test ###\\n53:     ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\\n54:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\\n55: \\n56: ### Running a particular unit/integration test with log4j output ###\\n57: By default, there will be only small number of logs output while testing. You can adjust it by changing the `log4j.properties` file in the module's `src/test/resources` directory.\\n58: \\n59: For example, if you want to see more logs for clients project tests, you can modify [the line](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties#L21) in `clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties` \\n60: to `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO` and then run:\\n61:     \\n62:     ./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest   \\n63: \\n64: And you should see `INFO` level logs in the file under the `clients/build/test-results/test` directory.\\n65: \\n66: ### Specifying test retries ###\\n67: By default, each failed test is retried once up to a maximum of five retries per test run. Tests are retried at the end of the test task. Adjust these parameters in the following way:\\n68: \\n69:     ./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\\n70:     \\n71: See [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\\n72: \\n73: ### Generating test coverage reports ###\\n74: Generate coverage reports for the whole project:\\n75: \\n76:     ./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\\n77: \\n78: Generate coverage for a single module, i.e.: \\n79: \\n80:     ./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\\n81:     \\n82: ### Building a binary release gzipped tar ball ###\\n83:     ./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\\n84: \\n85: The release file can be found inside `./core/build/distributions/`.\\n86: \\n87: ### Building auto generated messages ###\\n88: Sometimes it is only necessary to rebuild the RPC auto-generated message data when switching between branches, as they could\\n89: fail due to code changes. We set the `release` parameter in javac and scalac\n8: to `8` to ensure the generated binaries are compatible with Java 8 or higher (independently of the Java version\n9: used for compilation). Java 8 support project-wide has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.0, Java 11 support for\n10: the broker and tools has been deprecated since Apache Kafka 3.7 and removal of both is planned for Apache Kafka 4.0 (\n11: see [KIP-750](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308223) and\n12: [KIP-1013](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=284789510) for more details).\n13: \n14: Scala 2.12 and 2.13 are supported and 2.13 is used by default. Scala 2.12 support has been deprecated since\n15: Apache Kafka 3.0 and will be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0 (see [KIP-751](https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/pages/viewpage.action?pageId=181308218)\n16: for more details). See below for how to use a specific Scala version or all of the supported Scala versions.\n17: \n18: ### Build a jar and run it ###\n19:     ./gradlew jar\n20: \n21: Follow instructions in https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart\n22: \n23: ### Build source jar ###\n24:     ./gradlew srcJar\n25: \n26: ### Build aggregated javadoc ###\n27:     ./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\n28: \n29: ### Build javadoc and scaladoc ###\n30:     ./gradlew javadoc\n31:     ./gradlew javadocJar # builds a javadoc jar for each module\n32:     ./gradlew scaladoc\n33:     ./gradlew scaladocJar # builds a scaladoc jar for each module\n34:     ./gradlew docsJar # builds both (if applicable) javadoc and scaladoc jars for each module\n35: \n36: ### Run unit/integration tests ###\n37:     ./gradlew test # runs both unit and integration tests\n38:     ./gradlew unitTest\n39:     ./gradlew integrationTest\n40:     \n41: ### Force re-running tests without code change ###\n42:     ./gradlew test --rerun\n43:     ./gradlew unitTest --rerun\n44:     ./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\n45: \n46: ### Running a particular unit/integration test ###\n47:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\n48: \n49: ### Repeatedly running a particular unit/integration test ###\n50:     I=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \"Completed run: $I\"; sleep 1; done\n51: \n52: ### Running a particular test method within a unit/integration test ###\n53:     ./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\n54:     ./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\n55: \n56: ### Running a particular unit/integration test with log4j output ###\n57: By default, there will be only small number of logs output while testing. You can adjust it by changing the `log4j.properties` file in the module's `src/test/resources` directory.\n58: \n59: For example, if you want to see more logs for clients project tests, you can modify [the line](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties#L21) in `clients/src/test/resources/log4j.properties` \n60: to `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO` and then run:\n61:     \n62:     ./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest   \n63: \n64: And you should see `INFO` level logs in the file under the `clients/build/test-results/test` directory.\n65: \n66: ### Specifying test retries ###\n67: By default, each failed test is retried once up to a maximum of five retries per test run. Tests are retried at the end of the test task. Adjust these parameters in the following way:\n68: \n69:     ./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=1 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=5\n70:     \n71: See [Test Retry Gradle Plugin](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for more details.\n72: \n73: ### Generating test coverage reports ###\n74: Generate coverage reports for the whole project:\n75: \n76:     ./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n77: \n78: Generate coverage for a single module, i.e.: \n79: \n80:     ./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n81:     \n82: ### Building a binary release gzipped tar ball ###\n83:     ./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\n84: \n85: The release file can be found inside `./core/build/distributions/`.\n86: \n87: ### Building auto generated messages ###\n88: Sometimes it is only necessary to rebuild the RPC auto-generated message data when switching between branches, as they could\n89: fail due to code changes. You can just run:\n90:  \n91:     ./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\n92: \n93: ### Running a Kafka broker in KRaft mode\n94: \n95: Using compiled files:\n96: \n97:     KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID=\"$(./bin/kafka-storage.sh random-uuid)\"\n98:     ./bin/kafka-storage.sh format -t $KAFKA_CLUSTER_ID -c config/kraft/server.properties\n99:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/kraft/server.properties\n100: \n101: Using docker image:\n102: \n103:     docker run -p 9092:9092 apache/kafka:3.7.0\n104: \n105: ### Running a Kafka broker in ZooKeeper mode\n106: \n107: Using compiled files:\n108: \n109:     ./bin/zookeeper-server-start.sh config/zookeeper.properties\n110:     ./bin/kafka-server-start.sh config/server.properties\n111: \n112: >Since ZooKeeper mode is already deprecated and planned to be removed in Apache Kafka 4.0, the docker image only supports running in KRaft mode\n113: \n114: ### Cleaning the build ###\n115:     ./gradlew clean\n116: \n117: ### Running a task with one of the Scala versions available (2.12.x or 2.13.x) ###\n118: *Note that if building the jars with a version other than 2.13.x, you need to set the `SCALA_VERSION` variable or change it in `bin/kafka-run-class.sh` to run the quick start.*\n119: \n120: You can pass either the major version (eg 2.12) or the full version (eg 2.12.7):\n121: \n122:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\n123:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 test\n124:     ./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 releaseTarGz\n125: \n126: ### Running a task with all the scala versions enabled by default ###\n127: \n128: Invoke the `gradlewAll` script followed by the task(s):\n129: \n130:     ./gradlewAll test\n131:     ./gradlewAll jar\n132:     ./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\n133: \n134: ### Running a task for a specific project ###\n135: This is for `core`, `examples` and `clients`\n136: \n137:     ./gradlew core:jar\n138:     ./gradlew core:test\n139: \n140: Streams has multiple sub-projects, but you can run all the tests:\n141: \n142:     ./gradlew :streams:testAll\n143: \n144: ### Listing all gradle tasks ###\n145:     ./gradlew tasks\n146: \n147: ### Building IDE project ####\n148: *Note that this is not strictly necessary (IntelliJ IDEA has good built-in support for Gradle projects, for example).*\n149: \n150:     ./gradlew eclipse\n151:     ./gradlew idea\n152: \n153: The `eclipse` task has been configured to use `${project_dir}/build_eclipse` as Eclipse's build directory. Eclipse's default\n154: build directory (`${project_dir}/bin`) clashes with Kafka's scripts directory and we don't use Gradle's build directory\n155: to avoid known issues with this configuration.\n156: \n157: ### Publishing the jar for all versions of Scala and for all projects to maven ###\n158: The recommended command is:\n159: \n160:     ./gradlewAll publish\n161: \n162: For backwards compatibility, the following also works:\n163: \n164:     ./gradlewAll uploadArchives\n165: \n166: Please note for this to work you should create/update project, one cannot use gradle to upload to maven; instead the `mvn deploy` command needs to be called at the quickstart folder:\n177: \n178:     cd streams/quickstart\n179:     mvn deploy\n180: \n181: Please note for this to work you should create/update user maven settings (typically, `${USER_HOME}/.m2/settings.xml`) to assign the following variables\n182: \n183:     <settings xmlns=\"http://maven.apache.org/SETTINGS/1.0.0\"\n184:        xmlns:xsi=\"http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance\"\n185:        xsi:schemaLocation=\"http://maven.apache.org/SETTINGS/1.0.0\n186: ./gradlewAll publishToMavenLocal\n209: \n210: For backwards compatibility, the following also works:\n211: \n212:     ./gradlewAll install\n213: \n214: ### Installing specific projects to the local ### Building the test jar ###\n221:     ./gradlew testJar\n222: \n223: ### Running code quality checks ###\n224: There are two code quality analysis tools that we regularly run, spotbugs and checkstyle.\n225: \n226: #### Checkstyle ####\n227: Checkstyle enforces a consistent coding style in Kafka.\n228: You can run checkstyle using:\n229: \n230:     ./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\n231: \n232: The checkstyle warnings will be found in `reports/checkstyle/reports/main.html` and `reports/checkstyle/reports/test.html` files in the\n233: subproject build directories. They are also printed to the console. The build will fail if Checkstyle fails.\n234: \n235: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessCheck` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\n236: \n237: #### Spotless ####\n238: The import order is a part of static check. please call `spotlessApply` (require JDK 11+) to optimize the imports of Java codes before filing pull request.\n239: \n240:     ./gradlew spotlessApply\n241: \n242: **Please note that `./gradlew spotlessApply` currently has an issue with Java 21 (see https://github.com/diffplug/spotless/pull/1920), so make sure to run this with JDK 11 or 17**\n243: \n244: #### Spotbugs ####\n245: Spotbugs uses static analysis to look for bugs in the code.\n246: You can run spotbugs using:\n247: \n248:     ./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\n249: \n250: The spotbugs warnings will be found in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `reports/spotbugs/test.html` files in the subproject build\n251: directories.  Use -PxmlSpotBugsReport=true to generate an XML report instead of an HTML one.\n252: \n253: ### JMH microbenchmarks ###\n254: We use [JMH](https://openjdk.java.net/projects/code-tools/jmh/) to write microbenchmarks that produce reliable results in the JVM.\n255:     \n256: See [jmh-benchmarks/README.md](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/jmh-benchmarks/README.md) for details on how to run the microbenchmarks.\n257: \n258: ### Dependency Analysis ###\n259: \n260: The gradle [dependency debugging documentation](https://docs.gradle.org/current/userguide/viewing_debugging_dependencies.html) mentions using the `dependencies` or `dependencyInsight` tasks to debug dependencies for the root project or individual subprojects.\n261: \n262: Alternatively, use the `allDeps` or `allDepInsight` tasks for recursively iterating through all subprojects:\n263: \n264:     ./gradlew allDeps\n265: \n266:     ./gradlew allDepInsight --configuration runtimeClasspath --dependency com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind\n267: \n268: These take the same arguments as the builtin variants.\n269: \n270: ### Determining if any dependencies could be updated ###\n271:     ./gradlew dependencyUpdates\n272: \n273: ### Common build options ###\n274: \n275: The following options should be set with a `-P` switch, for example `./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=1 test`.\n276: \n277: * `commitId`: sets the build commit ID as .git/HEAD might not be correct if there are local commits added for build purposes.\n278: * `mavenUrl`: sets the URL of the maven deployment repository (`file://path/to/repo` can be used to point to a local repository).\n279: * `maxParallelForks`: maximum number of test processes to start in parallel. Defaults to the number of processors available to the JVM.\n280: * `maxScalacThreads`: maximum number of worker threads for the scalac backend. Defaults to the lowest of `8` and the number of processors\n281: available to the JVM. The value must be between 1 and 16 (inclusive). \n282: * `ignoreFailures`: ignore test failures from junit\n283: * `showStandardStreams`: shows standard out and standard error of the test JVM(s) on the console.\n284: * `skipSigning`: skips signing of artifacts.\n285: * `testLoggingEvents`: unit test events to be logged, separated by comma. For example `./gradlew -PtestLoggingEvents=started,passed,skipped,failed test`.\n286: * `xmlSpotBugsReport`: enable XML reports for spotBugs. This also disables HTML reports as only one can be enabled at a time.\n287: * `maxTestRetries`: maximum number of retries for a failing test case.\n288: * `maxTestRetryFailures`: maximum number of test failures before retrying is disabled for subsequent tests.\n289: * `enableTestCoverage`: enables test coverage plugins and tasks, including bytecode enhancement of classes required to track said\n290: coverage. Note that this introduces some overhead when running tests and hence why it's disabled by default (the overhead\n291: varies, but 15-20% is a reasonable estimate).\n292: * `keepAliveMode`: configures the keep alive mode for the Gradle compilation daemon - reuse improves start-up time. The values should \n293: be one of `daemon` or `session` (the default is `daemon`). `daemon` keeps the daemon alive until it's explicitly stopped while\n294: `session` keeps it alive until the end of the build session. This currently only affects the Scala compiler, see\n295: https://github.com/gradle/gradle/pull/21034 for a PR that attempts to do the same for the Java compiler.\n296: * `scalaOptimizerMode`: configures the optimizing behavior of the scala compiler, the value should be one of `none`, `method`, `inline-kafka` or\n297: `inline-scala` (the default is `inline-kafka`). `none` is the scala compiler default, which only eliminates unreachable code. `method` also\n298: includes method-local optimizations. `inline-kafka` adds inlining of methods within the kafka packages. Finally, `inline-scala` also\n299: includes inlining of methods within the scala library (which avoids lambda allocations for methods like `Option.exists`). `inline-scala` is\n300: only safe if the Scala library version is the same at compile time and runtime. Since we cannot guarantee this for all cases (for example, users\n301: may depend on the kafka jar for integration tests where they may include a scala library with a different version), we don't enable it by\n302: default. See https://www.lightbend.com/blog/scala-inliner-optimizer for more details.\n303: \n304: ### Running system tests ###\n305: \n306: See [tests/README.md](tests/README.md).\n307: \n308: ### Running in Vagrant ###\n309: \n310: See [vagrant/README.md](vagrant/README.md).\n311: \n312: ### Contribution ###\n313: \n314: Apache Kafka is interested in building the community; we would welcome any thoughts or [patches](https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA). You can reach us [on the Apache mailing lists](http://kafka.apache.org/contact.html).\n315: \n316: To contribute follow the instructions here:\n317:  * https://kafka.apache.org/contributing.html \n318: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--3.9.0@5010d340da347c7e58d0b503d83a5a892a29c127/-/blob/README.md"}}}

This can be done by running\\n15: ```\\n16: ./gradlew clean systemTestLibs\\n17: ```\\n18: * Run all tests\\n19: ```\\n20: bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n21: ```\\n22: * Run all tests with debug on (warning will produce log of logs)\\n23: ```\\n24: _DUCKTAPE_OPTIONS=\\\"--debug\\\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh | tee debug_logs.txt\\n25: ```\\n26: * Run a subset of tests\\n27: ```\\n28: TC_PATHS=\\\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams tests/kafkatest/tests/tools\\\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n29: ```\\n30: * Run a specific tests file\\n31: ```\\n32: TC_PATHS=\\\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py\\\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n33: ```\\n34: * Run a specific test class\\n35: ```\\n36: TC_PATHS=\\\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py::PluggableConsumerTest\\\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n37: ```\\n38: * Run a specific test method\\n39: ```\\n40: TC_PATHS=\\\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py::PluggableConsumerTest.test_start_stop\\\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n41: ```\\n42: * Run a specific test method with specific parameters\\n43: ```\\n44: TC_PATHS=\\\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams/streams_upgrade_test.py::StreamsUpgradeTest.test_metadata_upgrade\\\" _DUCKTAPE_OPTIONS='--parameters '\\\\''{\\\"from_version\\\":\\\"0.10.1.1\\\",\\\"to_version\\\":\\\"2.6.0-SNAPSHOT\\\"}'\\\\' bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n45: ```\\n46: * Run tests with a different JVM\\n47: ```\\n48: bash tests/docker/ducker-ak up -j 'openjdk:11'; tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n49: ```\\n50: * Remove ducker-ak containers\\n51: ```\\n52: bash tests/docker/ducker-ak down -f\\n53: ```\\n54: * Rebuild first and then run tests\\n55: ```\\n56: REBUILD=\\\"t\\\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\\n57: ```\\n58: * Run tests with Kafka in `native` mode\\n59:   - To run tests with Kafka in `native` mode, pass `{\\\"kafka_mode\\\": \\\"native\\\"}` to the ducktape globals. This can be done by running\n15: ```\n16: ./gradlew clean systemTestLibs\n17: ```\n18: * Run all tests\n19: ```\n20: bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n21: ```\n22: * Run all tests with debug on (warning will produce log of logs)\n23: ```\n24: _DUCKTAPE_OPTIONS=\"--debug\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh | tee debug_logs.txt\n25: ```\n26: * Run a subset of tests\n27: ```\n28: TC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams tests/kafkatest/tests/tools\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n29: ```\n30: * Run a specific tests file\n31: ```\n32: TC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n33: ```\n34: * Run a specific test class\n35: ```\n36: TC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py::PluggableConsumerTest\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n37: ```\n38: * Run a specific test method\n39: ```\n40: TC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py::PluggableConsumerTest.test_start_stop\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n41: ```\n42: * Run a specific test method with specific parameters\n43: ```\n44: TC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams/streams_upgrade_test.py::StreamsUpgradeTest.test_metadata_upgrade\" _DUCKTAPE_OPTIONS='--parameters '\\''{\"from_version\":\"0.10.1.1\",\"to_version\":\"2.6.0-SNAPSHOT\"}'\\' bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n45: ```\n46: * Run tests with a different JVM\n47: ```\n48: bash tests/docker/ducker-ak up -j 'openjdk:11'; tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n49: ```\n50: * Remove ducker-ak containers\n51: ```\n52: bash tests/docker/ducker-ak down -f\n53: ```\n54: * Rebuild first and then run tests\n55: ```\n56: REBUILD=\"t\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n57: ```\n58: * Run tests with Kafka in `native` mode\n59:   - To run tests with Kafka in `native` mode, pass `{\"kafka_mode\": \"native\"}` to the ducktape globals. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Nd4ESQEEgT9qbwsUgbvyXG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01ER5LU4qHVqTphRv33uYe5c","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/onboarding.md","content":"# Apache Kafka Contributor Guide\n\nThis guide provides step-by-step instructions for contributing to Apache Kafka, from building the project to submitting your changes for review.\n\n## 1. Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Requirements\n- **Git**: For cloning and managing the repository\n- **Java**: Multiple versions supported\n  - Java 8, 11, 17, and 21 are all tested and supported\n  - Java 8 support deprecated since Kafka 3.0; planned removal in 4.0\n  - Java 11 broker/tools support deprecated since Kafka 3.7\n  - Default: Use Java 11 or 17 for best experience\n\n### Scala Support\n- **Scala 2.12** and **2.13** are supported\n  - Scala 2.13 is the default\n  - Scala 2.12 support deprecated since Kafka 3.0; planned removal in 4.0\n- Both versions can be used by passing `-PscalaVersion=2.12` or `-PscalaVersion=2.13`\n\n### Required Tools\n- **Gradle**: The build system (managed via `./gradlew` wrapper)\n- **Maven**: Required for Kafka Streams quickstart archetype testing\n\n### Optional Tools for Code Quality\n- Code quality checks use **Checkstyle** and **SpotBugs** (automatically run during builds)\n- **Spotless** (requires JDK 11+) for import ordering and formatting\n\n---\n\n## 2. Gradle Build System\n\nKafka uses Gradle as its build system. The project is organized as a multi-project build with the following major modules:\n\n### Main Modules\n- `clients` - Kafka producer/consumer client libraries\n- `core` - Kafka broker and server components\n- `streams` - Kafka Streams framework (and sub-projects)\n- `connect` - Kafka Connect framework\n- `tools` - Command-line tools\n- `server`, `server-common`, `group-coordinator`, `transaction-coordinator` - Coordinator and server components\n- `storage`, `metadata`, `raft` - Storage and replication components\n- `shell` - Shell/REPL support\n- `examples` - Example applications\n- `jmh-benchmarks` - Performance microbenchmarks\n- `trogdor` - Workload generator for system tests\n\n### Key Gradle Commands\n\n#### Building\n```bash\n# Build JAR artifacts\n./gradlew jar\n\n# Build source JAR\n./gradlew srcJar\n\n# Build Javadoc (all modules)\n./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\n\n# Build documentation\n./gradlew javadoc                    # Javadoc\n./gradlew scaladoc                   # Scaladoc\n./gradlew javadocJar                 # Javadoc JARs for each module\n./gradlew scaladocJar                # Scaladoc JARs for each module\n./gradlew docsJar                    # Both javadoc and scaladoc JARs\n```\n\n#### Module-Specific Builds\n```bash\n# Build specific module (e.g., clients)\n./gradlew clients:jar\n./gradlew clients:test\n\n# Streams sub-projects\n./gradlew :streams:testAll           # Run all Streams tests\n\n# Core module\n./gradlew core:jar\n./gradlew core:test\n```\n\n#### Scala Version Variants\n```bash\n# Build with specific Scala version (2.12 or 2.13)\n./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\n./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 test\n\n# Build with all supported Scala versions\n./gradlewAll test\n./gradlewAll jar\n./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\n```\n\n#### Message Code Generation\n```bash\n# Regenerate RPC message classes (needed when switching branches)\n./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\n```\n\n#### Release/Packaging\n```bash\n# Build binary release tarball\n./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\n# Output: core/build/distributions/\n\n# Publish to local Maven repository\n./gradlewAll publishToMavenLocal\n\n# Publish to Maven central/snapshot repository\n./gradlewAll publish\n```\n\n#### IDE Support\n```bash\n# Generate IDE project files (optional - IntelliJ has good Gradle support)\n./gradlew eclipse\n./gradlew idea\n```\n\n#### Dependency Analysis\n```bash\n# List all dependencies for the project\n./gradlew allDeps\n\n# Check specific dependency insights\n./gradlew allDepInsight --configuration runtimeClasspath --dependency com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind\n\n# Check for dependency updates\n./gradlew dependencyUpdates\n```\n\n### Important Build Options\n\nPass these using `-P` flag (e.g., `./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=2 test`):\n\n- `commitId`: Custom git commit ID (overrides .git/HEAD)\n- `mavenUrl`: Maven repository URL for publishing\n- `maxParallelForks`: Max parallel test processes (default: number of available processors)\n- `maxScalacThreads`: Scala compiler threads (default: min(8, processors), range: 1-16)\n- `ignoreFailures`: Continue on test failures\n- `showStandardStreams`: Show test stdout/stderr on console\n- `skipSigning`: Skip artifact signing\n- `testLoggingEvents`: Test events to log (e.g., `started,passed,skipped,failed`)\n- `xmlSpotBugsReport`: Generate XML SpotBugs reports instead of HTML\n- `maxTestRetries`: Max test retries on failure (default: 1)\n- `maxTestRetryFailures`: Max test failures before disabling retries (default: 5)\n- `enableTestCoverage`: Enable test coverage (adds ~15-20% overhead)\n- `keepAliveMode`: Gradle daemon keep-alive mode (`daemon` or `session`)\n- `scalaOptimizerMode`: Scala optimizer level (`none`, `method`, `inline-kafka`, `inline-scala`)\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nKafka uses **JUnit 5 (Jupiter)** as the testing framework with **Mockito** for mocking.\n\n### Unit and Integration Tests\n\n#### Run All Tests\n```bash\n./gradlew test                       # Both unit and integration tests\n./gradlew unitTest                   # Unit tests only\n./gradlew integrationTest            # Integration tests only\n```\n\n#### Run Tests for a Specific Module\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test\n./gradlew core:test\n./gradlew streams:test               # Or use :streams:testAll for all Streams tests\n```\n\n#### Run a Specific Test Class\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\n./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest\n```\n\n#### Run a Specific Test Method\n```bash\n./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\n./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\n```\n\n#### Repeatedly Run a Test\n```bash\nI=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \"Completed run: $I\"; sleep 1; done\n```\n\n#### Re-run Tests Without Code Changes\n```bash\n./gradlew test --rerun\n./gradlew unitTest --rerun\n./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\n```\n\n#### Configure Test Logging\nBy default, minimal logs are shown. Modify test configuration:\n\n1. Edit `src/test/resources/log4j.properties` in the module\n2. Change log level (e.g., `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO`)\n3. Run tests with output redirection:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest\n```\n\nLogs appear in `<module>/build/test-results/test/` directory.\n\n#### Test Retry Configuration\n```bash\n# Customize retry behavior\n./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=2 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=10\n```\n\nSee [Test Retry Gradle Plugin docs](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for details.\n\n### Test Coverage\n\n```bash\n# Generate coverage report for entire project\n./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n\n# Generate coverage for specific module\n./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n```\n\n### System Integration Tests\n\nSystem tests use **ducktape** (distributed testing framework) and can be run with Docker:\n\n#### Prerequisites\n```bash\n# Build Kafka and system test libraries\n./gradlew clean systemTestLibs\n```\n\n#### Run All System Tests\n```bash\nbash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Subset of Tests\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Specific Test File\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Specific Test Class\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py::PluggableConsumerTest\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Specific Test Method\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams/streams_upgrade_test.py::StreamsUpgradeTest.test_metadata_upgrade\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Debug System Tests\n```bash\n# Run with debug logging\n_DUCKTAPE_OPTIONS=\"--debug\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh | tee debug_logs.txt\n\n# Run in VS Code debugger (attach mode)\ntests/docker/ducker-ak up\ntests/docker/ducker-ak test tests/kafkatest/tests/core/security_test.py --debug\n```\n\n#### Manage Docker Containers\n```bash\n# Start containers\nbash tests/docker/ducker-ak up\n\n# Start with native Kafka binary\nbash tests/docker/ducker-ak up -m native\n\n# Stop containers\nbash tests/docker/ducker-ak down -f\n```\n\nSee [tests/README.md](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/tests/README.md) for full details.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Code Quality Checks\n\n### Checkstyle\nEnsures consistent coding style:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\n```\n\nReports appear in `reports/checkstyle/reports/main.html` and `test.html` in each module's build directory.\n\n⚠️ **Note**: `spotlessCheck` has issues with Java 21; run with JDK 11 or 17.\n\n### Spotless (Import Ordering)\nOptimize import statements in Java code:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew spotlessApply\n```\n\n⚠️ **Note**: `spotlessApply` also has issues with Java 21; run with JDK 11 or 17.\n\n### SpotBugs\nStatic analysis to find potential bugs:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\n```\n\nReports in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `test.html`. Use `-PxmlSpotBugsReport=true` for XML output.\n\n### Run All Checks\nBefore submitting PR:\n```bash\n./gradlew check -x test          # All checks except tests\n./gradlew spotlessApply          # Fix import ordering (JDK 11/17 only)\n./gradlew test                   # Run all tests\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. CI Pipeline\n\n### Jenkins (Primary)\nApache Kafka uses **Jenkins** for the main CI pipeline.\n\n**Location**: Jenkins file at repository root: `Jenkinsfile`\n\n**Pipeline Overview**:\nThe build matrix tests across multiple Java and Scala versions in parallel:\n\n1. **JDK 8 + Scala 2.12**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - All unit and integration tests\n   - Kafka Streams archetype validation\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n2. **JDK 11 + Scala 2.13**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - Tests only on dev branches\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n3. **JDK 17 + Scala 2.13**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - Tests only on dev branches\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n4. **JDK 21 + Scala 2.13**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - All unit and integration tests\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n**Key Jenkins Tasks**:\n- `check -x test`: Code quality checks (SpotBugs, Checkstyle)\n- `test`: All unit and integration tests\n- Archetype test: Validates Kafka Streams quickstart artifact\n- Email notifications to `dev@kafka.apache.org` on failures\n\n**Build Scan**: Kafka uses [Gradle Enterprise](https://ge.apache.org) for build analytics.\n\n### GitHub Actions (Docker/Release)\nGitHub Actions handles Docker image builds and releases:\n- Docker image build and test (`.github/workflows/docker_build_and_test.yml`)\n- Official Docker image builds (`.github/workflows/docker_official_image_build_and_test.yml`)\n- Release promotion (`.github/workflows/docker_promote.yml`)\n- RC release builds (`.github/workflows/docker_rc_release.yml`)\n\n### Pull Request Checks\nAll pull requests undergo:\n1. **Validation Stage**: Code quality checks (SpotBugs, Checkstyle, import ordering)\n2. **Test Stage**:\n   - Unit and integration tests across Java versions\n   - Test output parsed and reported as JUnit XML\n3. **Archetype Test** (JDK 8 only): Validates Kafka Streams Maven archetype\n4. **Build Artifacts**: Profiles and build scans available in Jenkins\n\n---\n\n## 6. Code Review Process\n\n### Finding and Claiming Issues\n\n1. **Browse JIRA**: Issues tracked at https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n   - Filter by status: `Open` (not yet assigned)\n   - Filter by component area (clients, broker, streams, etc.)\n   - Look for `good-first-issue` label for beginner contributions\n\n2. **Claim the Issue**:\n   - Log in with Apache account (create if needed)\n   - Click \"Assign to me\" on the JIRA ticket\n   - Leave a comment indicating you'll work on it\n\n3. **Review Related KIPs**: Some changes require a Kafka Improvement Proposal (KIP)\n   - Check JIRA for linked KIPs at https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA\n   - Read KIP discussion for design rationale\n\n### Branch Naming\nWhile not strictly enforced, consider using:\n- `KAFKA-XXXXX` (issue number) as branch name for clarity\n- Example: `git checkout -b KAFKA-16428`\n\n### Creating a Pull Request\n\n1. **Prepare Your Work**:\n   ```bash\n   # Make sure your branch is up-to-date\n   git fetch upstream\n   git rebase upstream/main\n\n   # Run local checks before pushing\n   ./gradlew check spotlessApply\n   ./gradlew test\n   ```\n\n2. **Commit Your Changes**:\n   - Write clear, concise commit messages\n   - Reference the JIRA issue: `KAFKA-XXXXX; Brief description`\n   - One logical change per commit\n   - Include `Co-Authored-By` trailers for team work\n\n3. **Push and Create PR**:\n   ```bash\n   git push origin KAFKA-XXXXX\n   ```\n\n4. **Fill the PR Template** (auto-populated from `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`):\n   - **Title**: Should be suitable as commit message\n   - **Description**:\n     - Link to JIRA issue\n     - Explain what changed and why\n     - Summary of testing strategy (unit, integration, or system tests added)\n   - **Testing Checklist**:\n     - [ ] Unit tests added/modified\n     - [ ] Integration tests added/modified\n     - [ ] System tests considered (for larger changes)\n     - [ ] Documentation updated\n   - **Committer Checklist** (for review):\n     - Verify design and implementation\n     - Verify test coverage and CI\n     - Verify documentation\n\n### Code Review Expectations\n\n#### What Reviewers Look For\n- **Correctness**: Code logic is correct and handles edge cases\n- **Testing**: Adequate unit, integration, or system tests included\n- **Performance**: No regressions; benchmarks considered for performance-critical code\n- **API Design**: Backwards compatible or justified breaking changes\n- **Documentation**: Code comments and user-facing docs are clear\n- **Style**: Follows Kafka conventions (Checkstyle passes)\n- **JMH Benchmarks**: Added for performance-sensitive changes\n\n#### Getting Review\n- Kafka committers are volunteers; be patient\n- Tag reviewers if known (@username in PR)\n- Ask in [dev mailing list](http://kafka.apache.org/contact.html) for visibility\n- Small, focused PRs get reviewed faster\n\n#### Addressing Feedback\n- Push new commits to the same branch (don't force-push)\n- Respond to all comments\n- Re-request review after making changes\n- Iterations are normal; don't be discouraged\n\n#### Merge\n- Committer will squash commits and apply PR title as commit message\n- PR must pass all CI checks before merge\n- Must have at least one approval from a committer\n- Merged to `main` branch\n\n---\n\n## 7. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Scenario: Fix a Bug in the Producer Client\n\n#### Step 1: Find and Claim the Issue\n```bash\n# Browse https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n# Find issue KAFKA-16428: \"Producer fails with null pointer in edge case\"\n# Click \"Assign to me\"\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Set Up Your Local Environment\n```bash\n# Clone if you haven't already\ngit clone https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\ncd kafka\n\n# Add upstream if forking\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\n\n# Create and checkout feature branch\ngit fetch upstream\ngit checkout -b KAFKA-16428 upstream/main\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Understand the Issue\n- Read the JIRA description carefully\n- Check if there's a linked KIP\n- Review related code and tests\n- Reproduce the bug locally if possible\n\n#### Step 4: Implement the Fix\n```bash\n# Edit relevant files (e.g., clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/...)\n# Add/modify code and write unit tests\n\n# Example: Writing a test\n# File: clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerTest.java\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Run Local Tests\n```bash\n# Test the specific module\n./gradlew clients:test --tests ProducerTest\n\n# Run code quality checks\n./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck spotlessApply\n\n# Run broader test suite\n./gradlew clients:test\n\n# If it's a critical path, run longer tests\n./gradlew test -PmaxParallelForks=1\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Verify Your Changes Compile\n```bash\n# Clean build to catch any issues\n./gradlew clean clients:jar\n\n# Check for dependency issues\n./gradlew allDeps\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Commit Your Work\n```bash\n# Stage your changes\ngit add clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Producer.java\ngit add clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerTest.java\n\n# Write a clear commit message\ngit commit -m \"KAFKA-16428; Fix null pointer exception in Producer\n\n- Added null check in processCallback method\n- Added unit test to verify edge case handling\n- Verified no performance regression\"\n```\n\n#### Step 8: Push to Your Fork\n```bash\n# If forking\ngit push origin KAFKA-16428\n\n# Or push to a personal fork\ngit push https://github.com/<your-username>/kafka.git KAFKA-16428\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Create Pull Request\n1. Go to https://github.com/apache/kafka\n2. Click \"New Pull Request\"\n3. Choose your branch and fill the template:\n\n```\n## Description\n\nThis PR fixes KAFKA-16428: Producer fails with null pointer in edge case.\n\n### Changes\n- Added null check in `Producer.processCallback()` to handle case where\n  callback is null due to concurrent modification\n- Validates fix doesn't break existing functionality\n\n### Testing\n- Added `ProducerTest.testProcessCallbackWithNull()` unit test\n- Ran full `clients:test` suite: 234 tests pass\n- No regressions in performance benchmarks\n\n### Committer Checklist\n- [ ] Verify design and implementation\n- [ ] Verify test coverage and CI build status\n- [ ] Verify documentation (if needed)\n```\n\n#### Step 10: Address Code Review\n```bash\n# Reviewer suggests: \"Add javadoc to the new null-handling code\"\n\n# Make the change\n# Edit Producer.java and add javadoc\n\ngit add clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Producer.java\ngit commit -m \"KAFKA-16428; Add javadoc for null check in processCallback\"\ngit push origin KAFKA-16428\n\n# GitHub will auto-update the PR\n# Re-request review in PR conversation\n```\n\n#### Step 11: Wait for Merge\n- CI pipeline runs automatically\n- Committer reviews and approves\n- Once approved, committer merges to main\n- Your commit is squashed and merged\n\n#### Step 12: Clean Up\n```bash\n# Switch back to main\ngit checkout main\n\n# Pull latest changes\ngit pull upstream main\n\n# Delete your branch locally and on remote\ngit branch -d KAFKA-16428\ngit push origin --delete KAFKA-16428\n```\n\n---\n\n## Build Prerequisites\n\n### System Requirements\n- **Git**: For cloning and managing the repository\n- **Java**: Multiple versions supported\n  - Java 8, 11, 17, and 21 are all tested and supported\n  - Java 8 support deprecated since Kafka 3.0; planned removal in 4.0\n  - Java 11 broker/tools support deprecated since Kafka 3.7\n  - Default: Use Java 11 or 17 for best experience\n\n### Scala Support\n- **Scala 2.12** and **2.13** are supported\n  - Scala 2.13 is the default\n  - Scala 2.12 support deprecated since Kafka 3.0; planned removal in 4.0\n- Both versions can be used by passing `-PscalaVersion=2.12` or `-PscalaVersion=2.13`\n\n### Required Tools\n- **Gradle**: The build system (managed via `./gradlew` wrapper)\n- **Maven**: Required for Kafka Streams quickstart archetype testing\n\n### Optional Tools for Code Quality\n- Code quality checks use **Checkstyle** and **SpotBugs** (automatically run during builds)\n- **Spotless** (requires JDK 11+) for import ordering and formatting\n\n---\n\n## 2. Gradle Build System\n\nKafka uses Gradle as its build system. The project is organized as a multi-project build with the following major modules:\n\n### Main Modules\n- `clients` - Kafka producer/consumer client libraries\n- `core` - Kafka broker and server components\n- `streams` - Kafka Streams framework (and sub-projects)\n- `connect` - Kafka Connect framework\n- `tools` - Command-line tools\n- `server`, `server-common`, `group-coordinator`, `transaction-coordinator` - Coordinator and server components\n- `storage`, `metadata`, `raft` - Storage and replication components\n- `shell` - Shell/REPL support\n- `examples` - Example applications\n- `jmh-benchmarks` - Performance microbenchmarks\n- `trogdor` - Workload generator for system tests\n\n### Key Gradle Commands\n\n#### Building\n```bash\n# Build JAR artifacts\n./gradlew jar\n\n# Build source JAR\n./gradlew srcJar\n\n# Build Javadoc (all modules)\n./gradlew aggregatedJavadoc\n\n# Build documentation\n./gradlew javadoc                    # Javadoc\n./gradlew scaladoc                   # Scaladoc\n./gradlew javadocJar                 # Javadoc JARs for each module\n./gradlew scaladocJar                # Scaladoc JARs for each module\n./gradlew docsJar                    # Both javadoc and scaladoc JARs\n```\n\n#### Module-Specific Builds\n```bash\n# Build specific module (e.g., clients)\n./gradlew clients:jar\n./gradlew clients:test\n\n# Streams sub-projects\n./gradlew :streams:testAll           # Run all Streams tests\n\n# Core module\n./gradlew core:jar\n./gradlew core:test\n```\n\n#### Scala Version Variants\n```bash\n# Build with specific Scala version (2.12 or 2.13)\n./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 jar\n./gradlew -PscalaVersion=2.12 test\n\n# Build with all supported Scala versions\n./gradlewAll test\n./gradlewAll jar\n./gradlewAll releaseTarGz\n```\n\n#### Message Code Generation\n```bash\n# Regenerate RPC message classes (needed when switching branches)\n./gradlew processMessages processTestMessages\n```\n\n#### Release/Packaging\n```bash\n# Build binary release tarball\n./gradlew clean releaseTarGz\n# Output: core/build/distributions/\n\n# Publish to local Maven repository\n./gradlewAll publishToMavenLocal\n\n# Publish to Maven central/snapshot repository\n./gradlewAll publish\n```\n\n#### IDE Support\n```bash\n# Generate IDE project files (optional - IntelliJ has good Gradle support)\n./gradlew eclipse\n./gradlew idea\n```\n\n#### Dependency Analysis\n```bash\n# List all dependencies for the project\n./gradlew allDeps\n\n# Check specific dependency insights\n./gradlew allDepInsight --configuration runtimeClasspath --dependency com.fasterxml.jackson.core:jackson-databind\n\n# Check for dependency updates\n./gradlew dependencyUpdates\n```\n\n### Important Build Options\n\nPass these using `-P` flag (e.g., `./gradlew -PmaxParallelForks=2 test`):\n\n- `commitId`: Custom git commit ID (overrides .git/HEAD)\n- `mavenUrl`: Maven repository URL for publishing\n- `maxParallelForks`: Max parallel test processes (default: number of available processors)\n- `maxScalacThreads`: Scala compiler threads (default: min(8, processors), range: 1-16)\n- `ignoreFailures`: Continue on test failures\n- `showStandardStreams`: Show test stdout/stderr on console\n- `skipSigning`: Skip artifact signing\n- `testLoggingEvents`: Test events to log (e.g., `started,passed,skipped,failed`)\n- `xmlSpotBugsReport`: Generate XML SpotBugs reports instead of HTML\n- `maxTestRetries`: Max test retries on failure (default: 1)\n- `maxTestRetryFailures`: Max test failures before disabling retries (default: 5)\n- `enableTestCoverage`: Enable test coverage (adds ~15-20% overhead)\n- `keepAliveMode`: Gradle daemon keep-alive mode (`daemon` or `session`)\n- `scalaOptimizerMode`: Scala optimizer level (`none`, `method`, `inline-kafka`, `inline-scala`)\n\n---\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\nKafka uses **JUnit 5 (Jupiter)** as the testing framework with **Mockito** for mocking.\n\n### Unit and Integration Tests\n\n#### Run All Tests\n```bash\n./gradlew test                       # Both unit and integration tests\n./gradlew unitTest                   # Unit tests only\n./gradlew integrationTest            # Integration tests only\n```\n\n#### Run Tests for a Specific Module\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test\n./gradlew core:test\n./gradlew streams:test               # Or use :streams:testAll for all Streams tests\n```\n\n#### Run a Specific Test Class\n```bash\n./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest\n./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest\n```\n\n#### Run a Specific Test Method\n```bash\n./gradlew core:test --tests kafka.api.ProducerFailureHandlingTest.testCannotSendToInternalTopic\n./gradlew clients:test --tests org.apache.kafka.clients.MetadataTest.testTimeToNextUpdate\n```\n\n#### Repeatedly Run a Test\n```bash\nI=0; while ./gradlew clients:test --tests RequestResponseTest --rerun --fail-fast; do (( I=$I+1 )); echo \"Completed run: $I\"; sleep 1; done\n```\n\n#### Re-run Tests Without Code Changes\n```bash\n./gradlew test --rerun\n./gradlew unitTest --rerun\n./gradlew integrationTest --rerun\n```\n\n#### Configure Test Logging\nBy default, minimal logs are shown. Modify test configuration:\n\n1. Edit `src/test/resources/log4j.properties` in the module\n2. Change log level (e.g., `log4j.logger.org.apache.kafka=INFO`)\n3. Run tests with output redirection:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew cleanTest clients:test --tests NetworkClientTest\n```\n\nLogs appear in `<module>/build/test-results/test/` directory.\n\n#### Test Retry Configuration\n```bash\n# Customize retry behavior\n./gradlew test -PmaxTestRetries=2 -PmaxTestRetryFailures=10\n```\n\nSee [Test Retry Gradle Plugin docs](https://github.com/gradle/test-retry-gradle-plugin) for details.\n\n### Test Coverage\n\n```bash\n# Generate coverage report for entire project\n./gradlew reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n\n# Generate coverage for specific module\n./gradlew clients:reportCoverage -PenableTestCoverage=true -Dorg.gradle.parallel=false\n```\n\n### System Integration Tests\n\nSystem tests use **ducktape** (distributed testing framework) and can be run with Docker:\n\n#### Prerequisites\n```bash\n# Build Kafka and system test libraries\n./gradlew clean systemTestLibs\n```\n\n#### Run All System Tests\n```bash\nbash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Subset of Tests\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Specific Test File\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Specific Test Class\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/client/pluggable_test.py::PluggableConsumerTest\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Run Specific Test Method\n```bash\nTC_PATHS=\"tests/kafkatest/tests/streams/streams_upgrade_test.py::StreamsUpgradeTest.test_metadata_upgrade\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh\n```\n\n#### Debug System Tests\n```bash\n# Run with debug logging\n_DUCKTAPE_OPTIONS=\"--debug\" bash tests/docker/run_tests.sh | tee debug_logs.txt\n\n# Run in VS Code debugger (attach mode)\ntests/docker/ducker-ak up\ntests/docker/ducker-ak test tests/kafkatest/tests/core/security_test.py --debug\n```\n\n#### Manage Docker Containers\n```bash\n# Start containers\nbash tests/docker/ducker-ak up\n\n# Start with native Kafka binary\nbash tests/docker/ducker-ak up -m native\n\n# Stop containers\nbash tests/docker/ducker-ak down -f\n```\n\nSee [tests/README.md](https://github.com/apache/kafka/blob/trunk/tests/README.md) for full details.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Code Quality Checks\n\n### Checkstyle\nEnsures consistent coding style:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck\n```\n\nReports appear in `reports/checkstyle/reports/main.html` and `test.html` in each module's build directory.\n\n⚠️ **Note**: `spotlessCheck` has issues with Java 21; run with JDK 11 or 17.\n\n### Spotless (Import Ordering)\nOptimize import statements in Java code:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew spotlessApply\n```\n\n⚠️ **Note**: `spotlessApply` also has issues with Java 21; run with JDK 11 or 17.\n\n### SpotBugs\nStatic analysis to find potential bugs:\n\n```bash\n./gradlew spotbugsMain spotbugsTest -x test\n```\n\nReports in `reports/spotbugs/main.html` and `test.html`. Use `-PxmlSpotBugsReport=true` for XML output.\n\n### Run All Checks\nBefore submitting PR:\n```bash\n./gradlew check -x test          # All checks except tests\n./gradlew spotlessApply          # Fix import ordering (JDK 11/17 only)\n./gradlew test                   # Run all tests\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. CI Pipeline\n\n### Jenkins (Primary)\nApache Kafka uses **Jenkins** for the main CI pipeline.\n\n**Location**: Jenkins file at repository root: `Jenkinsfile`\n\n**Pipeline Overview**:\nThe build matrix tests across multiple Java and Scala versions in parallel:\n\n1. **JDK 8 + Scala 2.12**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - All unit and integration tests\n   - Kafka Streams archetype validation\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n2. **JDK 11 + Scala 2.13**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - Tests only on dev branches\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n3. **JDK 17 + Scala 2.13**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - Tests only on dev branches\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n4. **JDK 21 + Scala 2.13**\n   - Validation (checks except tests)\n   - All unit and integration tests\n   - Timeout: 8 hours\n\n**Key Jenkins Tasks**:\n- `check -x test`: Code quality checks (SpotBugs, Checkstyle)\n- `test`: All unit and integration tests\n- Archetype test: Validates Kafka Streams quickstart artifact\n- Email notifications to `dev@kafka.apache.org` on failures\n\n**Build Scan**: Kafka uses [Gradle Enterprise](https://ge.apache.org) for build analytics.\n\n### GitHub Actions (Docker/Release)\nGitHub Actions handles Docker image builds and releases:\n- Docker image build and test (`.github/workflows/docker_build_and_test.yml`)\n- Official Docker image builds (`.github/workflows/docker_official_image_build_and_test.yml`)\n- Release promotion (`.github/workflows/docker_promote.yml`)\n- RC release builds (`.github/workflows/docker_rc_release.yml`)\n\n### Pull Request Checks\nAll pull requests undergo:\n1. **Validation Stage**: Code quality checks (SpotBugs, Checkstyle, import ordering)\n2. **Test Stage**:\n   - Unit and integration tests across Java versions\n   - Test output parsed and reported as JUnit XML\n3. **Archetype Test** (JDK 8 only): Validates Kafka Streams Maven archetype\n4. **Build Artifacts**: Profiles and build scans available in Jenkins\n\n---\n\n## 6. Code Review Process\n\n### Finding and Claiming Issues\n\n1. **Browse JIRA**: Issues tracked at https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n   - Filter by status: `Open` (not yet assigned)\n   - Filter by component area (clients, broker, streams, etc.)\n   - Look for `good-first-issue` label for beginner contributions\n\n2. **Claim the Issue**:\n   - Log in with Apache account (create if needed)\n   - Click \"Assign to me\" on the JIRA ticket\n   - Leave a comment indicating you'll work on it\n\n3. **Review Related KIPs**: Some changes require a Kafka Improvement Proposal (KIP)\n   - Check JIRA for linked KIPs at https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/KAFKA\n   - Read KIP discussion for design rationale\n\n### Branch Naming\nWhile not strictly enforced, consider using:\n- `KAFKA-XXXXX` (issue number) as branch name for clarity\n- Example: `git checkout -b KAFKA-16428`\n\n### Creating a Pull Request\n\n1. **Prepare Your Work**:\n   ```bash\n   # Make sure your branch is up-to-date\n   git fetch upstream\n   git rebase upstream/main\n\n   # Run local checks before pushing\n   ./gradlew check spotlessApply\n   ./gradlew test\n   ```\n\n2. **Commit Your Changes**:\n   - Write clear, concise commit messages\n   - Reference the JIRA issue: `KAFKA-XXXXX; Brief description`\n   - One logical change per commit\n   - Include `Co-Authored-By` trailers for team work\n\n3. **Push and Create PR**:\n   ```bash\n   git push origin KAFKA-XXXXX\n   ```\n\n4. **Fill the PR Template** (auto-populated from `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`):\n   - **Title**: Should be suitable as commit message\n   - **Description**:\n     - Link to JIRA issue\n     - Explain what changed and why\n     - Summary of testing strategy (unit, integration, or system tests added)\n   - **Testing Checklist**:\n     - [ ] Unit tests added/modified\n     - [ ] Integration tests added/modified\n     - [ ] System tests considered (for larger changes)\n     - [ ] Documentation updated\n   - **Committer Checklist** (for review):\n     - Verify design and implementation\n     - Verify test coverage and CI\n     - Verify documentation\n\n### Code Review Expectations\n\n#### What Reviewers Look For\n- **Correctness**: Code logic is correct and handles edge cases\n- **Testing**: Adequate unit, integration, or system tests included\n- **Performance**: No regressions; benchmarks considered for performance-critical code\n- **API Design**: Backwards compatible or justified breaking changes\n- **Documentation**: Code comments and user-facing docs are clear\n- **Style**: Follows Kafka conventions (Checkstyle passes)\n- **JMH Benchmarks**: Added for performance-sensitive changes\n\n#### Getting Review\n- Kafka committers are volunteers; be patient\n- Tag reviewers if known (@username in PR)\n- Ask in [dev mailing list](http://kafka.apache.org/contact.html) for visibility\n- Small, focused PRs get reviewed faster\n\n#### Addressing Feedback\n- Push new commits to the same branch (don't force-push)\n- Respond to all comments\n- Re-request review after making changes\n- Iterations are normal; don't be discouraged\n\n#### Merge\n- Committer will squash commits and apply PR title as commit message\n- PR must pass all CI checks before merge\n- Must have at least one approval from a committer\n- Merged to `main` branch\n\n---\n\n## 7. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Scenario: Fix a Bug in the Producer Client\n\n#### Step 1: Find and Claim the Issue\n```bash\n# Browse https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA\n# Find issue KAFKA-16428: \"Producer fails with null pointer in edge case\"\n# Click \"Assign to me\"\n```\n\n#### Step 2: Set Up Your Local Environment\n```bash\n# Clone if you haven't already\ngit clone https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\ncd kafka\n\n# Add upstream if forking\ngit remote add upstream https://github.com/apache/kafka.git\n\n# Create and checkout feature branch\ngit fetch upstream\ngit checkout -b KAFKA-16428 upstream/main\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Understand the Issue\n- Read the JIRA description carefully\n- Check if there's a linked KIP\n- Review related code and tests\n- Reproduce the bug locally if possible\n\n#### Step 4: Implement the Fix\n```bash\n# Edit relevant files (e.g., clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/...)\n# Add/modify code and write unit tests\n\n# Example: Writing a test\n# File: clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerTest.java\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Run Local Tests\n```bash\n# Test the specific module\n./gradlew clients:test --tests ProducerTest\n\n# Run code quality checks\n./gradlew checkstyleMain checkstyleTest spotlessCheck spotlessApply\n\n# Run broader test suite\n./gradlew clients:test\n\n# If it's a critical path, run longer tests\n./gradlew test -PmaxParallelForks=1\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Verify Your Changes Compile\n```bash\n# Clean build to catch any issues\n./gradlew clean clients:jar\n\n# Check for dependency issues\n./gradlew allDeps\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Commit Your Work\n```bash\n# Stage your changes\ngit add clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Producer.java\ngit add clients/src/test/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerTest.java\n\n# Write a clear commit message\ngit commit -m \"KAFKA-16428; Fix null pointer exception in Producer\n\n- Added null check in processCallback method\n- Added unit test to verify edge case handling\n- Verified no performance regression\"\n```\n\n#### Step 8: Push to Your Fork\n```bash\n# If forking\ngit push origin KAFKA-16428\n\n# Or push to a personal fork\ngit push https://github.com/<your-username>/kafka.git KAFKA-16428\n```\n\n#### Step 9: Create Pull Request\n1. Go to https://github.com/apache/kafka\n2. Click \"New Pull Request\"\n3. Choose your branch and fill the template:\n\n```\n## Description\n\nThis PR fixes KAFKA-16428: Producer fails with null pointer in edge case.\n\n### Changes\n- Added null check in `Producer.processCallback()` to handle case where\n  callback is null due to concurrent modification\n- Validates fix doesn't break existing functionality\n\n### Testing\n- Added `ProducerTest.testProcessCallbackWithNull()` unit test\n- Ran full `clients:test` suite: 234 tests pass\n- No regressions in performance benchmarks\n\n### Committer Checklist\n- [ ] Verify design and implementation\n- [ ] Verify test coverage and CI build status\n- [ ] Verify documentation (if needed)\n```\n\n#### Step 10: Address Code Review\n```bash\n# Reviewer suggests: \"Add javadoc to the new null-handling code\"\n\n# Make the change\n# Edit Producer.java and add javadoc\n\ngit add clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Producer.java\ngit commit -m \"KAFKA-16428; Add javadoc for null check in processCallback\"\ngit push origin KAFKA-16428\n\n# GitHub will auto-update the PR\n# Re-request review in PR conversation\n```\n\n#### Step 11: Wait for Merge\n- CI pipeline runs automatically\n- Committer reviews and approves\n- Once approved, committer merges to main\n- Your commit is squashed and merged\n\n#### Step 12: Clean Up\n```bash\n# Switch back to main\ngit checkout main\n\n# Pull latest changes\ngit pull upstream main\n\n# Delete your branch locally and on remote\ngit branch -d KAFKA-16428\ngit push origin --delete KAFKA-16428\n```\n\n---\n\n##
